    <div class="section">
      

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_234713515">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/234713515" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/4238592-sarah-s-reviews" class="left imgcol" title="Sarah's Reviews"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1283531041p2/4238592.jpg" alt="Sarah's Reviews" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/234713515?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Apr 08, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4238592-sarah-s-reviews" class="user" title="Sarah's Reviews">Sarah's Reviews</a>

          added it


          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/11312.Over_Sea_Under_Stone" title="Paperback 9780689871214" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer234713515">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13870466712319082879">When Simon, Jane, and Barney found an old manuscript while on holiday, they had no idea that it would put them in the center of the timeless struggle between good and the dark. Now they must race to discover where the manuscript leads before the agents of the dark can find out and it's too late.<br /><br />Over Sea, Under Stone is the first of five books in The Dark is Rising Sequence. It's a light read aimed at elementary school age readers. The<br />story contains some mildly scary situations, something like hy</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText13870466712319082879">When Simon, Jane, and Barney found an old manuscript while on holiday, they had no idea that it would put them in the center of the timeless struggle between good and the dark. Now they must race to discover where the manuscript leads before the agents of the dark can find out and it's too late.<br /><br />Over Sea, Under Stone is the first of five books in The Dark is Rising Sequence. It's a light read aimed at elementary school age readers. The<br />story contains some mildly scary situations, something like hypnotism, keeping information from parents, and at least one instance where it is implied that someone said a not nice word. There is no profanity (in English at least), sexual content, killing, or real violence.<br /><br />Interesting Note: The tone and beginning reminded me strongly of C.S. Lewis' The Lion, The Witch, and The Wardrobe and there are several similarities early on – although the stories are actually quite different.<br /><br />To read more content based reviews visit <a rel="nofollow" href="http://ssbookreviews.blogspot.com/">Sarah's Reviews</a>.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="13870466712319082879">...more</a>

          </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/268660131?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 27, 2012</a>

      <a href="/user/show/223837-nikki" class="user" title="Nikki">Nikki</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/223837-nikki?shelf=children-s-and-ya" class="actionLinkLite">children-s-and-ya</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/223837-nikki?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer268660131">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14478648652964665014">It's going to become difficult to find editions of these books I haven't read, sooner or later. I'm not sure that there's anything much to say about these books that I haven't already said. I read it this time with an appreciation for the pace, and the sense of fear that genuinely comes across. It's not as fully developed as the later books in the sequence, but she manages to create a pretty fully realised world where people act like people and the dark may also be the Dark. I know that it creep</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14478648652964665014">It's going to become difficult to find editions of these books I haven't read, sooner or later. I'm not sure that there's anything much to say about these books that I haven't already said. I read it this time with an appreciation for the pace, and the sense of fear that genuinely comes across. It's not as fully developed as the later books in the sequence, but she manages to create a pretty fully realised world where people act like people and the dark may also be the Dark. I know that it creeped me out when I was a kid: less so now, but there's still the little twinge of wanting to pull my feet in under the covers so no one can grab them...<br /><br />Mostly, I reread these books for the characters. Barney, Simon and Jane feel like real people to me now, I've read these books so often, and I've missed them. This is the most simplistic of the books, but I couldn't imagine the sequence without it.</span>

        <a href="/review/show/4689384?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Aug 17, 2007</a>

      <a href="/user/show/37712-yi" class="user" title="Yi">Yi</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

              <a href="/review/list/37712-yi?shelf=justread" class="actionLinkLite">justread</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer4689384">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11317503470313667826">I saw Susan Cooper speak at a writer's conference back in February and have been meaning to read this sequence ever since then. (Never mind that the rest of the conference only had me itching to get back to my keyboard.) <br />If you haven't yet read The Chronicles of Narnia, you'll love love love this book. If you've already read it, you'll still love this book. Its characters are ever so much more engaging than Edmund, Lucy, Peter, and Susan are, and although the basic premise of good versus evil is</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText11317503470313667826">I saw Susan Cooper speak at a writer's conference back in February and have been meaning to read this sequence ever since then. (Never mind that the rest of the conference only had me itching to get back to my keyboard.) <br />If you haven't yet read The Chronicles of Narnia, you'll love love love this book. If you've already read it, you'll still love this book. Its characters are ever so much more engaging than Edmund, Lucy, Peter, and Susan are, and although the basic premise of good versus evil is still the backbone of the book, it's ever so much more believable than the Chronicles. All the action takes place in our very real world, although I don't know if the same will hold true as the series progresses.<br />The language in this book is well crafted, although I also don't know if that's because I hear Cooper's voice in my head as I'm reading. :) Enjoy!</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer959374796239523994">Chronologically and sequentially the first in "The Dark is Rising" series. Years ago, the great librarian at Jefferson Elementary in San Francisco told me I should know about these books, and I finally have gotten around to them. For children and adults who are fans of "Harry Potter" or other literature grounded in Arthurian and English myth, they are must-reads. "Over Sea, Under Stone" introduces the reader to Simon, Jane and Barney Drew (as well as their mysterious uncle Merriman) and a quest</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText959374796239523994">Chronologically and sequentially the first in "The Dark is Rising" series. Years ago, the great librarian at Jefferson Elementary in San Francisco told me I should know about these books, and I finally have gotten around to them. For children and adults who are fans of "Harry Potter" or other literature grounded in Arthurian and English myth, they are must-reads. "Over Sea, Under Stone" introduces the reader to Simon, Jane and Barney Drew (as well as their mysterious uncle Merriman) and a quest for the Grail. Superb.</span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('e1Ilsc7ekN5nw08bSPku3tgiMfu5PRw7i35G07u8G+CzLGbzVFLwROD7UDzUU7wME9aDcGPjFo2j2yEzNaZ2/A==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('UK/2Q2QyZNYTMP2ya7346wynBQzJ8wmrNQJy6KgRys2Y0bUB/r4ETJQI4pX3F2o5x1O3hxMtAx0dpxUIJgun0Q==')})

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/7308.Susan_Cooper">About Susan Cooper</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/7308.Susan_Cooper"><img alt="7308" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1379606336p2/7308.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer17186532427120366871">Susan Cooper's latest book is the YA novel "Ghost Hawk" (2013)<br /><br />Susan Cooper was born in 1935, and grew up in England's Buckinghamshire, an area that was green countryside then but has since become part of Greater London. As a child, she loved to read, as did her younger brother, who also became a writer. After attending Oxford, where she became the first woman to ever edit that university's newspap</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText17186532427120366871">Susan Cooper's latest book is the YA novel "Ghost Hawk" (2013)<br /><br />Susan Cooper was born in 1935, and grew up in England's Buckinghamshire, an area that was green countryside then but has since become part of Greater London. As a child, she loved to read, as did her younger brother, who also became a writer. After attending Oxford, where she became the first woman to ever edit that university's newspaper, Cooper worked as a reporter and feature writer for London's Sunday Times; her first boss was James Bond creator Ian Fleming.<br /><br />Cooper wrote her first book for young readers in response to a publishing house competition; "Over Sea, Under Stone" would later form the basis for her critically acclaimed five-book fantasy sequence, "The Dark Is Rising." The fourth book in the series, "The Grey King," won the Newbery Medal in 1976. By that time, Susan Cooper had been living in America for 13 years, having moved to marry her first husband, an American professor, and was stepmother to three children and the mother of two.<br /><br />Cooper went on to write other well-received novels, including "The Boggart" (and its sequel "The Boggart and the Monster"), "King of Shadows", and "Victory," as well as several picture books for young readers with illustrators such as Ashley Bryan and Warwick Hutton. She has also written books for adults, as well as plays and Emmy-nominated screenplays, many in collaboration with the actor Hume Cronyn, whom she married in 1996. Hume Cronyn died in 2003 and Ms. Cooper now lives in Marshfield MA. When Cooper is not working, she enjoys playing piano, gardening, and traveling.<br /><br />Recent books include the collaborative project "The Exquisite Corpse Adventure" and her biography of Jack Langstaff titled "The Magic Maker." Her newest book is "Ghost Hawk."<br /><br />Visit her Facebook pages: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/SusanCooperFanPage" target="_blank">www.facebook.com/SusanCooperFanPage</a><br /><a rel="nofollow" href="http://www.facebook.com/GhostHawkBySusanCooper" target="_blank">www.facebook.com/GhostHawkBySusanCooper</a><br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="17186532427120366871">...more</a>

    </div>

Good against evil.”</span>
